{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_BOUNDARY_SETTING_VIA_ANECDOTE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The boundary between psychological control and physiological pathology in hypnosis", "tone_constraint": "Pragmatic, clinical, humble yet authoritative, and grounded in observation", "structural_constraint": "Definition of boundary -> Vivid clinical anecdote (psychosomatic) -> Admission of mystery -> Therapeutic approach -> Clear exclusion of organic pathology"}, "instruction": "Explain the limits of hypnotic influence on the body by contrasting a psychosomatic response with organic disease, using a clinical example to illustrate the power of the unconscious mind while maintaining professional realism.", "reasoning_trace": "I will begin by establishing a clear boundary: the 'psychological control of behavior.' To illustrate the depth of this control, I will use a concrete, slightly startling clinical observation—a patient inducing a nosebleed through purely psychological means. By admitting 'I don't know' how the physiological mechanism works, I shift the focus from the 'how' to the 'what' and 'why,' which is the therapist's domain. I will describe the therapeutic intervention as a matter-of-fact process (giving a Kleenex) followed by addressing the underlying 'willingness' or psychological motivation. Finally, I will draw a sharp contrast between these functional/psychosomatic responses and organic, physically pathological conditions like cancer. This serves to protect the integrity of the field by not overpromising and by distinguishing between what the mind can influence (behavioral/functional) and what it likely cannot (organic cellular pathology).", "output": "I’ll draw the line at psychological control of behavior. I do know that a patient can be sitting perfectly quietly in a chair in my office and be in need of sympathy, and so develop a nosebleed without lifting a hand to his face. How did he do it? I don’t know. But I simply give him a Kleenex and proceed to work on that problem: I get the patient unwilling to do that kind of thing again, and then I try to find out why he was willing to do it in the first place. But as for treating actual, physically pathological failings like cancer, hypnotically, I don’t think it can be done. I can’t see any reason for thinking that it could."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_CONTEXT", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Redefining rapport to include environmental factors", "tone_constraint": "Respectful critique, observational, grounded in immediate sensory experience", "structural_constraint": "Compliment -> Pivot -> Concrete Observation -> Broadened Definition"}, "instruction": "Critique a narrow definition of rapport and expand it to include the subject's relationship with their entire environment, using the current physical setting as an example.", "reasoning_trace": "To redefine rapport, I must first validate the existing discourse to maintain social rapport with the speaker. Then, I will use a 'utilization' approach by drawing the audience's attention to their immediate, undeniable physical reality—the chairs, the desks, the ceiling. By demonstrating that we are always in 'relationship' with our surroundings, I logically extend the concept of hypnotic rapport to include the entire environmental context. This bypasses the intellectual resistance to a new definition by making it a self-evident observation of the present moment. The goal is to move from a rigid, dyadic definition to a holistic, situational one that allows the therapist to utilize the entire environment in the hypnotic process.", "output": "Dr. Pattie gave an extremely interesting talk, and yet I want to take exception to some of his remarks. First, he gave a definition of rapport as being the relationship between subject and hypnotist. But what is rapport? I think it is far more than [just what exists between subject and hypnotist, or between patient and hypnotherapist]. At the present time, all of you are sitting in this room in relationship to this desk, in relationship to a certain chair, in relationship to the people around you, in relationship to the ceiling, and so on. Rapport in hypnotic situations is not shown just in relationship to the operator; it also may be shown in relationship to the circumstances in which the hypnosis is done. And often, that is the case."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ANECDOTE_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Manifestation of catalepsy in clinical settings", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, narrative, and observational", "structural_constraint": "Anecdotal framing with rhetorical questioning and temporal contrast"}, "instruction": "Explain the subtle manifestation of catalepsy through a clinical anecdote, emphasizing the discrepancy between immediate diagnosis and prolonged observation.", "reasoning_trace": "I will begin by framing the concept of catalepsy not as a textbook definition, but as a living phenomenon to be observed. I'll use a narrative about psychiatric residents to create a 'surrogate' for the listener, allowing them to learn from the residents' experience. By contrasting the '30-second' instruction with 'two, long hours' of observation, I am inducing a state of focused attention and patience. I will describe mundane movements (combing hair, scratching) to build a false sense of normalcy, only to pivot to the 'awkward position' of the feet. This illustrates that catalepsy can be localized and subtle, bypassing the expectation of full-body rigidity. The rhetorical questions serve to anchor the diagnosis in the listener's mind as an inevitable conclusion of careful observation.", "output": "Catalepsy was another phenomenon discussed. Now how do people show catalepsy? Perhaps I can cite an example to illustrate the answer. A while back, I called my psychiatric residents into the staff room and I brought in a patient for them to deal with. I sat the patient down in a chair, and I let the residents sit there for two, long hours while she looked out the window, combed her hair, scratched her head, scratched her shoulder, and so forth. I had told the residents before she arrived that they should each make a final diagnosis within the first 30 seconds of observing her. So we sat there for two, long hours. What was the diagnosis?—catatonic schizophrenia. And what was characteristic of her?—her catalepsy. For those two hours she kept her feet in an extremely awkward position, but that was the only part of her body that showed catalepsy."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_OBSERVATIONAL_REDEFINITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Manifestation of catalepsy in unexpected body parts", "tone_constraint": "Educational, clinical yet conversational, observant", "structural_constraint": "Rhetorical question followed by specific physiological observations and a concluding synthesis."}, "instruction": "Explain how catalepsy can manifest in subtle or unexpected ways during hypnosis, using specific physiological examples like eye or neck movements to broaden the observer's definition of the phenomenon.", "reasoning_trace": "To effectively teach the recognition of trance states, I must first disrupt the student's narrow expectation that catalepsy only occurs in the limbs. I begin with a rhetorical question that shifts focus from the 'expected' (arm) to the 'unexpected'. Then, I provide vivid, sensory-based descriptions of eyeball rigidity and neck stiffness. By describing the mechanics—moving the head instead of the eyes—I anchor the concept in observable reality. Finally, I unify these disparate observations under the clinical label of 'catalepsy', thereby expanding the practitioner's diagnostic lens and validating the presence of trance even when it doesn't look 'textbook'.", "output": "How often does a hypnotic subject show catalepsy not when you lift his arm as you may expect, but rather in some other, unexpected part of his body? I’ve seen catalepsy manifested by a rigidity of the eyeball movements, where subjects move their heads but they do not move their eyeballs. That is, if they want to look over in that direction, they turn their heads rather than moving their eyes. Or, subjects may move their eyes but hold their necks stiff. But they are all showing catalepsy."}

What are controlled experiments in, let us say, a nonsense syllable learning situation? It isn’t a controlled experiment if you have altered anything from one situation to the next. I find that it’s much more controlled when you have the same nonsense syllables, and when the experimenter was just as clean-shaven for the experiment as he is for the follow-up experiment two years later. Even the growing of a mustache is a very serious interference with recollection."}

And what difference does it make by what measure you approach that memory? What matters is that you are trying to find out what the memory is. So to put yourself in a totally different situation from the one associated with the memory—even though you may not recognize that it is a totally different situation—interferes seriously [with your ability to recall it. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_SHOCK_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "극심한 통증을 겪는 말기 암 환자의 심리적 패턴 중단 및 통제권 확보", "tone_constraint": "충격적이고 직설적이며, 권위적이지만 정직한 어조", "structural_constraint": "환자의 두려움을 부정하지 않고 오히려 증폭시킨 뒤, 미세하게 조정(not too much)하며 종결하는 구조"}, "instruction": "극심한 고통 속에서 '아프게 하지 마세요'라고 반복하며 방어 기제를 세우는 환자에게, 일반적인 위로 대신 환자의 기대를 완전히 뒤엎는 충격 요법(Shock Therapy)을 사용하여 무의식적 주의를 집중시키고 치료적 주도권을 잡는 발언을 하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 환자는 이미 극심한 통증과 공포라는 '트랜스' 상태에 빠져 있으며, '아프게 하지 마세요'라는 말은 일반적인 위로가 통하지 않는 견고한 방어벽입니다. 둘째, 환자의 현실(고통에 대한 공포)을 부정하는 대신 이를 적극적으로 수용(Pacing)하고 오히려 강화함으로써 환자의 예상을 깨뜨리는 '패턴 중단(Pattern Interrupt)'을 시도합니다. 셋째, '지금보다 더 아프게 할 것'이라는 선언은 환자의 내부적 고통에 쏠려 있던 주의를 외부(의사)로 급격히 전환시킵니다. 넷째, '겁을 줄 것'이라는 솔직한 고백은 역설적으로 의사에 대한 신뢰를 형성하며, 마지막에 '너무 많이는 아니지만(Not too much)'이라는 단서를 붙임으로써 고통의 강도를 의사가 조절할 수 있다는 암시를 주어 통제권을 확보합니다.", "output": "I am going to hurt you, I really am going to hurt you. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The therapeutic necessity of discomfort and fear", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, clinical, yet collaborative and analytical", "structural_constraint": "Direct declarative statements followed by a series of open-ended, presuppositional questions"}, "instruction": "Explain to a patient that the therapeutic process will involve pain and fear, but frame it as a collaborative investigation into the specific parameters of that discomfort to facilitate healing.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I establish an unavoidable reality by using blunt, direct language ('I must hurt you'). This shock tactic bypasses the patient's conscious defenses by being unexpectedly honest. Second, I immediately shift the focus from the 'fact' of the pain to the 'variables' of the pain. By asking 'how much' and 'in what way,' I use the linguistic tool of presupposition—the patient's mind is forced to accept that pain will occur in order to process the question of its quantity. Third, I use the collective 'we' to transform the therapist from an aggressor into a collaborative researcher. This moves the patient from a state of passive fear to a state of active, analytical observation of their own experience. Finally, the repetition of the questions creates a rhythmic, hypnotic cadence that anchors the necessity of the process while maintaining a sense of therapeutic control.", "output": "But I must hurt you; I must scare you. What we’ve got to find out is, how much do I have to hurt you? How much do I have to scare you? In what way am I going to scare you? Why am I going to scare you?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DISSOCIATION_TRANCE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Mind-body dissociation for deep trance induction", "tone_constraint": "Rhythmic, repetitive, and authoritative yet permissive", "structural_constraint": "Contrastive structure using 'body' vs 'mind' and 'sleep' vs 'awake'"}, "instruction": "내담자가 신체적으로는 깊은 이완(잠) 상태에 들어가되, 정신적으로는 치료적 작업을 위해 명료하게 깨어 있도록 유도하는 해리(Dissociation) 기법 기반의 최면 암시를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 전체적인 상태를 '신체'와 '정신'이라는 두 가지 별개의 영역으로 분리(Dissociation)하는 전략을 세웁니다. '단지 신체만(just her body)'이라는 한정 표현을 통해 신체의 마비나 이완이 정신의 활동을 방해하지 않도록 경계를 설정합니다. 이러한 반복적이고 리드미컬한 대조는 내담자의 비판적 사고를 우회하고 깊은 트랜스 상태 내에서의 의사소통을 가능하게 합니다.", "output": "I told her to go to sleep, sound asleep; but in doing so she was to keep her mind wide awake; that her body was to go to sleep—just her body—but her mind was to remain wide awake."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_SYMPTOM_SUBSTITUTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Pain management through sensory displacement and substitution", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, repetitive, and sensory-focused", "structural_constraint": "Direct instruction combined with negative suggestion and intensification of a substitute sensation"}, "instruction": "내담자가 침대에서 몸을 뒤척일 때 느끼는 통증을 완화하기 위해, 통증 대신 발바닥에 아주 강렬한 가려움증을 느끼도록 유도하는 최면적 지시를 내리세요.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 주의 분산 및 부정 암시: '침대에서 뒤척이는 것을 생각할 필요가 없다'는 부정 암시를 통해, 역설적으로 그 행동이 고통스럽다는 사실을 상기시키면서 동시에 의식의 초점을 그 고통으로부터 떼어놓을 준비를 시킵니다. 2. 감각의 치환(Symptom Substitution): 견디기 힘든 통증을 '가려움증'이라는 다른 종류의 강렬한 감각으로 대체합니다. 이는 통증의 신경 신호를 가려움증이라는 덜 위협적인 신호로 덮어쓰기 하는 전략입니다. 3. 언어적 강화와 반복: 'horrible', 'terrible'과 같은 극단적인 형용사를 반복 사용하여 내담자의 무의식이 새로운 감각(가려움증)에 완전히 압도되도록 만듭니다. 이는 고통을 잊게 할 만큼 강력한 자극을 무의식적으로 생성하게 합니다. 4. 구체적 신체 부위 타겟팅: '오른쪽 발바닥'이라는 매우 구체적인 지점을 설정하여 암시의 구체성을 확보하고 내담자의 주의력을 한 곳으로 집중시킵니다. 5. 주도권 부여: '발달시키다(develop)', '만들다(make)'라는 동사를 사용하여 내담자가 자신의 신체 감각을 스스로 통제하고 생성할 수 있다는 무의식적 유능감을 심어줍니다.", "output": "There are certain things I want you to do. Second, I will introduce a circular physical metaphor—walking around the block—to mirror the circular nature of his thoughts but add the element of movement. Third, I will employ a technique of kinesthetic anchoring: assigning one side of the conflict (divorce) to the right foot and the other (staying married) to the left foot. This mechanical rhythm forces the unconscious to process the conflict as a physical sequence rather than an emotional deadlock. Fourth, I will use repetitive language ('round and around') to induce a light trance state. Finally, I will reframe the inevitable physical fatigue as a positive goal ('enjoy developing fatigue'), suggesting that physical exhaustion will naturally lead to the cessation of the mental debate and a restful state (sleep).", "output": "Why don’t you walk around the block, round and around and around—while you debate that question. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DIRECTIVE_CLOSURE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Physical exercise as a vehicle for mental resolution and sleep induction", "tone_constraint": "Pragmatic, authoritative, and finalistic", "structural_constraint": "Sequential tasking followed by a definitive psychological presupposition"}, "instruction": "Provide a concluding directive to a student who has been struggling with internal conflict, using a physical walking task to ensure both physical exhaustion and mental closure.", "reasoning_trace": "To facilitate a transition from mental rumination to physical rest, I first establish a preparatory phase ('Before you start out'). I use the concept of 'mapping out' to provide a sense of structure and control. By specifying a 'reasonable' yet 'long enough' walk, I utilize a physiological truism: sustained physical effort leads to tiredness. The 'so that' conjunctions serve as linguistic bridges, linking the physical act of walking directly to the desired outcomes of returning home and sleeping. Finally, I deliver the most crucial psychological intervention: 'You have thoroughly debated the question.' By stating this in the past perfect tense, I presuppose that the internal conflict is already resolved, effectively closing the mental 'file' and allowing the subject's unconscious to accept rest as the only logical next step.", "output": "Before you start out, first map out a reasonable walk, a long enough walk, so that you will feel tired at the end of it; so that you can come back to your apartment and go to bed. And if you view your problem honestly and comprehensively and earnestly—and I am going to say this to you in words that at first do not seem right—if you will view your problem, however distressing it is to you, there are certain pleasant aspects to it. There are also—and these are the things that brought you to me—unpleasant aspects to it. Now, what are these pleasant aspects?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reframing a physical symptom (emphysematous cough)", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative yet accepting, paradoxical, and gently leading", "structural_constraint": "Initial pacing of the symptom's severity followed by a shift to positive attributes using tag questions"}, "instruction": "내담자의 고통스러운 신체적 증상(기침)을 부정하지 않으면서도, 그 증상의 긍정적인 속성(강도, 깊이)을 찾아내어 관점을 전환(Reframing)시키는 대화형 최면 기법을 사용하여 말해보세요.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Pacing and Validation: 내담자가 느끼는 고통을 '끔찍한 기침'이라고 명확히 지칭함으로써 현재의 고통스러운 현실을 있는 그대로 인정(Pacing)하고 라포를 형성함. 2. Social Truism: '당신도 알고 나도 알고 모두가 놀란다'는 표현을 통해 내담자의 주관적 경험을 객관적 사실로 확증함. 3. Introduction of Curiosity: '즐거운 측면이 무엇일지 궁금해할 수 있다'는 표현으로 내담자의 의식적 저항을 우회하여 새로운 관점을 탐색하도록 유도함. 4. Contrast and Reframing: '얕고 효과 없는 기침'과 '깊고 강한 기침'을 대비시킴. 증상의 부정적 측면(고통)에서 기능적 측면(깊이와 힘)으로 초점을 옮김. 5. Tag Questions: '그렇지 않나요?(isn't it?)', '아니죠?(is it?)'와 같은 부가 의문문을 사용하여 내담자의 무의식적 동의를 이끌어내고 새로운 프레임을 고착화함. 6. Final Affirmation: '깊고, 좋고, 강한 기침'이라는 긍정적 형용사를 배치하여 증상에 대한 내담자의 정서적 반응을 재구조화함.", "output": "Now, that is a horrible, emphysematous cough that you have. You know it, I know it, everybody is alarmed by it. You can wonder what the pleasant aspect of it is, and it is rather a deep cough, isn’t it? It is not a shallow, ineffectual cough, is it? It is a rather deep, good, strong cough."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DISARMING_RESISTANCE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Approaching a migraine patient by decoupling hypnotic learning from therapeutic success.", "tone_constraint": "Skeptical, non-pressuring, experimental, and professionally humble.", "structural_constraint": "Initial negative suggestion followed by a conditional sequential process (Step A: Learning, Step B: Investigation)."}, "instruction": "Create a clinical dialogue for a patient with a chronic condition like migraines. Use a technique that lowers performance anxiety by expressing doubt about the ultimate cure while focusing the patient's attention on the immediate, neutral task of learning hypnosis as a separate skill.", "reasoning_trace": "To bypass the patient's resistance and fear of failure, I first utilize a 'negative suggestion' by stating I don't believe hypnosis will help. This aligns with any skepticism the patient may have, effectively 'joining' their resistance. I then shift the goal from 'therapy' (which carries the weight of expectation) to 'learning' ( a neutral process). By structuring the interaction as an experiment to see if they *can* learn, I remove the pressure to get well. I use a sequential logic: first, we master the trance; only then do we even consider the migraine. This 'fractionation of goals' ensures the patient's unconscious can engage in the trance state without the conscious mind's interference regarding the headache symptoms. Finally, I reiterate my uncertainty to maintain a low-pressure, collaborative atmosphere.", "output": "I don’t believe that hypnosis is going to help you, but what I would like to do is a rather simple thing of finding out if you can learn hypnosis. If you can learn hypnosis—after you have learned it—then we can investigate the possibility of using hypnosis for your migraine headache. I am not the least bit certain that we can, but let us find out if you can learn to go into a trance."}

'연령 퇴행의 가장 좋은 방법은 무엇인가?'라는 질문은 표면적으로는 지식을 묻는 것처럼 보이지만, 심리적으로는 청중의 뇌가 '퇴행'이라는 개념을 처리하기 위해 자신의 과거 기억이나 경험적 데이터베이스를 검색(Transderivational Search)하게 만듭니다. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REGRESSION_REVIVIFICATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Sensory-based memory regression and revivification", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, inquisitive, and progressively narrowing focus", "structural_constraint": "A sequence of five interconnected questions moving from the general environment to a specific sensory experience"}, "instruction": "내담자가 과거의 기억 속으로 자연스럽게 퇴행(regression)하여 당시의 감각을 생생하게 재경험(revivification)할 수 있도록, 일반적인 장소에서 시작하여 구체적인 시각적 세부 사항으로 주의를 좁혀가는 유도 질문을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨은 내담자의 의식적인 저항을 피하기 위해 직접적인 '기억해내라'는 명령 대신, 가벼운 호기심을 자극하는 질문 형식을 취합니다. 첫째, '어느 마을'이라는 넓은 범주의 질문으로 기억의 탐색을 시작합니다. 둘째, '현관(porch)'이라는 구체적인 물리적 구조물을 언급하여 기억의 공간적 좌표를 고정합니다. 셋째, '서향(west)'이라는 방향성을 제시하여 내담자가 머릿속에서 공간을 시각적으로 재구성하게 유도합니다. 넷째, '일몰을 보았다'는 행위를 결합하여 정적인 기억에 시간의 흐름과 움직임을 부여합니다. 마지막으로 '특정한 일몰'을 묻는 것은 내담자의 무의식이 가장 감정적 밀도가 높은 기억의 지점으로 스스로 도달하게 만드는 정교한 유도 장치입니다.", "output": "Whereabouts in a small village did you grow up? {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_AGE_REGRESSION_SPATIAL_ANCHORING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Age regression and sensory vividness in a sunset memory", "tone_constraint": "Calm, inquisitive, guiding, and matter-of-fact", "structural_constraint": "Interrogative sentences that presuppose the reality of the memory through spatial orientation"}, "instruction": "내담자가 과거의 기억으로 퇴행해 있는 상태에서, 그 기억의 생생함을 더하고 무의식적 몰입을 심화시키기 위해 공간적 위치를 묻는 질문을 던지세요.", "reasoning_trace": "내담자의 연령 퇴행(Age Regression)을 심화시키기 위해 에릭슨은 '전제(Presupposition)'의 기법을 사용합니다. 단순히 '부모님이 보이나요?'라고 묻는 대신, '어느 쪽에 앉아 계신가요?'라고 질문함으로써 부모님이 그 자리에 실재한다는 사실을 기정사실화합니다. 이러한 공간적 위치에 대한 질문은 내담자의 뇌가 내부 이미지를 3차원적으로 재구성하도록 강제하며, 이는 비판적 의식을 우회하여 무의식적 생생함(Vividness)을 극대화합니다. 또한, 질문의 형식을 빌려 내담자가 스스로 답을 찾게 함으로써 최면적 환각을 내담자 자신의 현실로 고착시키는 전략적 접근입니다.", "output": "And did anybody else sit on the porch with you? And how does that headache really feel now?"}

'How does it show itself?'라는 질문은 내담자의 주관적이고 모호한 느낌을 구체적인 '감각적 데이터'로 전환하도록 유도함. 3. 내담자가 남성임에도 불구하고 'morning sickness(입덧)'라는 여성적/임신 관련 증상을 호소할 때, 이를 생물학적 불가능성으로 지적하지 않고 그의 '주관적 진실'로 온전히 수용함(Utilization). 4. 이러한 수용은 내담자와의 강력한 라포를 형성하며, 무의식적 반응이 신체에 미치는 영향력을 인정함으로써 이후 최면적 암시가 작동할 수 있는 통로를 확보함.", "output": "선생님, 저는 지금 무언가를 품고(brooding) 있습니다. 그것이 당신에게 구체적으로 어떤 식으로 나타나고 있습니까? 아, 아침마다 입덧을 하시는군요."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ATTENTION_SHIFT", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Pain management through selective attention and sensory redirection", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, authoritative, and permissive with a focus on somatic sensations", "structural_constraint": "Postponing the negative symptom (pain) while prioritizing and layering positive sensory experiences (comfort, heaviness, relaxation)"}, "instruction": "신체적 통증을 호소하는 내담자에게, 통증에 대한 논의를 뒤로 미루고 신체의 편안한 부위에 집중하게 함으로써 무의식적인 이완을 유도하는 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 작성하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 호소하는 통증을 완전히 무시하지 않고 '나중에 다루겠다'는 약속을 통해 저항을 최소화(Acknowledge and Postpone)합니다. 그 다음 '하지만 먼저(but first)'라는 전환어를 사용하여 주의의 초점을 고통에서 편안함으로 즉각 이동시킵니다. '어디가 편안한가?'라는 질문은 신체 어딘가에는 반드시 편안한 곳이 있다는 전제(Presupposition)를 깔고 있어, 내담자의 무의식이 스스로 그 부위를 찾게 만듭니다. '이완', '무거움'과 같은 구체적인 감각 언어를 중첩시켜 트랜스 상태를 유도하며, 마지막으로 '너무 편안해서 움직이기 귀찮을 정도'라는 비유를 사용하여 의식적인 노력을 배제하고 깊은 신체적 안락함에 몰입하도록 유도합니다.", "output": "We will come to the question of the aches and the pain later, but first tell me where your body feels comfortable. Where do you feel relaxed? Where do you feel heavy? Where do you feel rather comfortable, as if you were too lazy to move from sheer comfort?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRECISION_INQUIRY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Feedback on clinical inquiry regarding TMJ pain", "tone_constraint": "Professional, inquisitive, subtly challenging, and sensory-oriented", "structural_constraint": "Initial validation followed by a series of increasingly specific, context-driven questions"}, "instruction": "치과 의사 친구가 아내의 턱관절 통증에 대해 질문한 방식에 대해 피드백을 제공하십시오. 단순히 증상을 묻는 것을 넘어, 통증이 발생하는 구체적인 맥락과 감각적 세부 사항(음식의 종류, 앉는 위치, 요일 등)을 생생하게 재구성하도록 유도하는 에릭슨의 대화 기법을 사용하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. [Validation & Rapport] 먼저 '매우 잘 물어보았다'는 칭찬으로 시작하여 상대방의 전문적 자존감을 세워주고 저항을 최소화함. 2. [Introducing the Concept of 'Situation'] '상황을 구축하다(build up the situation)'라는 표현을 통해, 단순히 정보를 얻는 것과 치료적 맥락을 형성하는 것의 차이를 암시함. 3. [Sensory Specificity] '교합(bite)'이라는 신체적 감각에서 시작하여 '스테이크', '로스트 비프'와 같은 구체적인 음식을 언급함. 이는 뇌가 통증을 추상적인 관념이 아닌 구체적인 감각적 사건으로 처리하게 함. 4. [Contextual Anchoring] 식탁의 위치나 요일과 같은 환경적 변수를 질문에 포함시킴으로써, 내담자(아내)가 자신의 고통을 둘러싼 무의식적 패턴을 스스로 탐색하게 유도함. 5. [Indirect Teaching] 친구에게 질문의 기술을 가르치는 동시에, 통증의 원인이 단순한 물리적 결함이 아닌 생활 양식과 연결되어 있을 수 있다는 관점을 간접적으로 주입함.", "output": "You know, I think you inquired into your wife’s pain very well, but did you really build up the situation for her? Did you get a very careful description of her bite, as well as she could give it? Did you ask her when she had that temporal mandibular pain? Was it when she was eating steak, or roast beef, or whatever? Where does she sit at the table? On what days of the week does the pain seem worse?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DISSOCIATIVE_SUBSTITUTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Managing physical discomfort through sensory substitution and dissociation", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, inquisitive, and gently leading", "structural_constraint": "Transitioning from a state of 'unawareness' to a specific 'alternative awareness' using rhetorical questions"}, "instruction": "고온의 실험실 환경에서 신체적 고통을 겪는 내담자에게, 현재의 신체 감각을 무시(Dissociation)하게 만들고 그 빈자리를 시원한 눈(snow)에 대한 생생한 기억으로 채우도록 유도하는 에릭슨식 최면 암시를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 현재 겪고 있는 '신체 감각의 상실'이라는 상태를 기정사실화(utilization)하며 시작합니다. 'Now, while you are losing your body awareness'라는 문구는 현재 진행 중인 해리 상태를 강화합니다. 그 다음, 단순히 열기를 잊으라고 명령하는 대신 '다른 종류의 인식(awareness of another kind)'이라는 모호한 가능성을 제시하여 내담자의 무의식이 스스로 대안을 찾게 유도합니다. 마지막으로 'Why not...?'이라는 허용적 질문 형식을 통해 저항을 최소화하면서, '눈 속을 걷는 것', '눈을 치우는 것'과 같은 구체적이고 운동감각적인(kinesthetic) 냉각 기억을 소환하도록 설계했습니다. 이는 고온이라는 현재의 실재를 무의식적 수준에서 냉기라는 과거의 기억으로 덮어쓰기(substitution)하려는 의도입니다.", "output": "Now, while you are losing your body awareness, what about this possibility of having an awareness of another kind? Why not have a wealth of memories of walking in the snow, of shoveling snow?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Symptom utilization instead of abolition", "tone_constraint": "Direct, paradoxical, and matter-of-fact", "structural_constraint": "Pacing the current physical sensation followed by a leading suggestion for functional reframing"}, "instruction": "내담자가 호소하는 신체적 통증이나 증상을 단순히 없애야 할 부정적인 것으로 치부하지 말고, 그것을 변화의 과정에서 유익하게 활용할 수 있는 자원으로 재정의하는 에릭슨적 개입을 수행하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 현재 느끼고 있는 감각적 실제(두통)를 명확하게 언급함으로써 '페이싱(Pacing)'을 수행합니다. 이는 내담자로 하여금 상담자가 자신의 상태를 정확히 이해하고 있다는 신뢰를 줍니다. 그 다음, 일반적인 기대(치료를 통한 통증 제거)를 깨뜨리는 '역설적 개입'을 시도합니다. '그것을 어떤 방식으로든 활용해야 한다(make some kind of use of it)'는 제안은 내담자의 의식적인 저항을 우회하며, 무의식으로 하여금 이 증상이 존재해야 하는 새로운 목적이나 해결책을 찾도록 유도합니다. 'ought to'라는 표현을 통해 부드러우면서도 단호한 권유를 전달하여 증상에 대한 내담자의 태도를 수동적 고통에서 능동적 활용으로 전환시킵니다.", "output": "Now, you have rather a bad headache there. I think you ought to make some kind of use of it."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_INDIRECT_INQUIRY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Establishing rapport and gathering unconscious material from a chronic patient with psychosomatic symptoms.", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, permissive, yet subtly authoritative with a focus on curiosity rather than clinical diagnosis.", "structural_constraint": "A simple, open-ended sentence using an auxiliary verb of obligation ('ought') to frame a permissive request."}, "instruction": "Generate a response for a patient who has seen many doctors for paralysis and expects you to 'suggest away' their symptoms. Use an indirect approach that shifts the focus from the symptom to the patient's subjective experience, building a bridge for the unconscious to reveal more information.", "reasoning_trace": "1. The patient arrives with a history of failed direct interventions; therefore, a direct suggestion to 'stop being paralyzed' would likely trigger the same resistance. 2. I must bypass the conscious expectation of a 'quick fix' by showing interest in the patient's total experience rather than just the pathology. 3. Using the word 'ought' provides a soft sense of clinical authority that the patient expects, but I apply it to the act of sharing rather than the act of healing. 4. By phrasing it as 'things that happen to you,' I am pacing the patient's experience of passivity (paralysis and absentmindedness are things that 'happen' to her), which validates her current state without judgment. 5. This creates a safe, non-confrontational space for the unconscious to begin communicating more freely, allowing me to gather the necessary psychological resources for later utilization.", "output": "You really ought to tell me some more of the things that happen to you."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_GRADATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Pain management through sensory shifting and utilization", "tone_constraint": "Validating, observational, and subtly directive", "structural_constraint": "Pacing current reality (hot burning) followed by leading to a new focus (periphery/warmth) and an open-ended utilization question"}, "instruction": "편두통을 앓고 있는 내담자에게 통증을 직접적으로 없애려 하기보다, 통증의 경계면에서 느껴지는 미세한 감각의 변화를 인지하게 하고 그 감각을 활용하도록 유도하는 에릭슨의 대화법을 구사하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 겪고 있는 '뜨겁고 타는 듯한 통증'이라는 주관적 현실을 'Yes'라는 긍정을 통해 수용(Pacing)하여 저항을 최소화합니다. 그 다음, 통증을 하나의 거대한 덩어리가 아닌 구조적인 실체로 분해하기 위해 '주변부(periphery)'라는 개념을 도입합니다. 강렬한 통증의 중심에서 벗어나 그 가장자리에 존재하는 '따스함(warm feeling)'과 '단계적 변화(gradation)'를 관찰하게 함으로써 내담자의 주의(Attention)를 고통에서 완화된 감각으로 전이시킵니다. 마지막으로, 이 새로운 감각을 어떻게 '사용(use)'할 것인지 묻는 개방형 질문을 던져, 내담자의 무의식이 스스로 통증을 조절하고 재구성하는 치유 프로세스에 참여하도록 유도합니다.", "output": "Yes, you have a hot burning sensation on the side of your head that always goes with your migraine headache. But, you know, if you will examine the periphery of that hot burning spot, there is a warm feeling, there is a gradation. Now how about the use of that warm feeling?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_SENSORY_SHIFT_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Pain management for arthritis through sensory reframing", "tone_constraint": "Calm, permissive, observant, and subtly directive", "structural_constraint": "Pacing the current reality, transitioning to sensory exploration, and suggesting the extension of neutral sensations"}, "instruction": "관절염 통증을 호소하는 내담자에게, 통증이라는 고정된 감각을 세부적인 온도 감각으로 분해하고 이를 확장하도록 유도하는 에릭슨 최면 기법을 사용하여 말해보세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 겪고 있는 고통과 의학적 진단(관절염)을 명확히 언급함으로써 현재의 고통스러운 현실을 페이싱(Pacing)하여 신뢰를 구축합니다. 그 다음, '통증'이라는 포괄적이고 부정적인 단어를 '감각(sensations)'이라는 중립적인 용어로 재정의(Reframing)합니다. '아마도(perhaps)'라는 허용적 단어를 사용하여 내담자가 자신의 감각을 스스로 탐색하게 유도하며, 통증 속에 숨겨진 따뜻함, 시원함, 차가움과 같은 구체적인 온도 감각들을 분리해내도록 합니다. 마지막으로, 이러한 중립적이거나 긍정적인 감각들을 '확장(extending)'해보라는 제안을 통해, 뇌가 통증 신호 대신 다른 감각에 집중하고 이를 증폭시킴으로써 자연스럽게 통증 완화를 경험하도록 유도하는 전략을 취합니다.", "output": "You have aching pains in your legs that distress you very greatly; you are suffering from arthritis. But if you will examine those sensations, you will find, perhaps, a feeling of warmth; perhaps a feeling of coolness; perhaps a feeling of coldness; and now how about extending some of those sensations?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reframing physical pain and stiffness as a protective biological mechanism.", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative yet reassuring, clinical but accessible, deeply validating of the unconscious body's wisdom.", "structural_constraint": "Start with a positive evaluation, use truisms about the patient's lack of knowledge to bypass conscious resistance, explain the physiological 'why' as a benefit, and conclude with a suggestion for a positive emotional response."}, "instruction": "내담자가 느끼는 신체적 통증과 뻣뻣함을 신체의 지혜로운 방어 기제로 재정의(Reframing)하여, 환자가 자신의 증상을 긍정적으로 수용하도록 유도하는 밀턴 에릭슨의 대화법을 구사하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Validate and Reframe: I begin by expressing pleasure ('I am awfully glad') at the symptom, which immediately disrupts the patient's negative expectation and creates a 'therapeutic double bind' where the symptom is now a sign of health. 2. Establish Unconscious Autonomy: By pointing out the patient's lack of medical or anatomical knowledge, I separate the conscious mind (which is ignorant and worried) from the unconscious body (which is wise and capable). 3. Explain the Mechanism (Splinting): I use the technical yet understandable concept of 'splinting' to explain muscle tension not as a malfunction, but as a deliberate, protective act to 'cut down the pain.' 4. Generalize and Normalize: I provide a simple physical analogy (hand and forearm) to make the global stiffness feel logical and inevitable ('of course'), reducing the patient's fear of the unknown. 5. Prescribe the Emotion: I conclude by suggesting the patient 'ought to be pleased,' effectively shifting the emotional valence of the pain from suffering to an appreciation of the body's adequacy.", "output": "I am awfully glad that your body is making so adequate a response. You really don’t know very much about medicine. You really don’t know very much about anatomy. You didn’t go to medical school, but you’ve got a backache and your body is automatically going to splint the back. It is going to tense the muscles in order to protect the back movements and cut down the pain. You splint the muscles in your hand, you notice your forearm tightens up too, and so, of course, you feel stiff all over. I think you ought to be pleased for that indication of the adequacy of your back muscles splinting the backache."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DOUBLE_BIND_RECIPROCITY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inviting subjects for a demonstration", "tone_constraint": "Playful, authoritative, and hypnotic", "structural_constraint": "Reciprocal double bind using interlocking questions"}, "instruction": "두 명의 청중을 무대로 불러내기 위해, 거절할 수 없는 이중 구속(Double Bind)과 상호 보완적 제안을 사용하여 최면적 유도를 수행하십시오. 피험자들의 외모에 대한 긍정적 수식어를 포함하여 저항을 최소화하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 피험자가 무대로 올라올지 말지에 대한 선택권을 주는 대신, '누가 누구를 데려올 것인가'라는 실행 방식에 초점을 맞추어 거절의 선택지를 원천 봉쇄하는 이중 구속 전략을 사용함. 둘째, 'pretty'라는 형용사를 반복 사용하여 피험자들에게 긍정적인 사회적 승인을 제공함으로써 제안에 대한 심리적 저항을 낮춤. 셋째, A가 B를 데려오고 B가 A를 데려온다는 상호 순환적 문장 구조를 통해 논리적 사고를 일시적으로 혼란시키고(Confusion Technique), 두 사람이 함께 움직여야 한다는 무의식적 의무감을 형성함. 넷째, 질문의 형식을 취하고 있으나 실제로는 행동을 유도하는 강력한 암시를 내포함.", "output": "Will the pretty blond bring the pretty brunette up? {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_INTERROGATIVE_INDUCTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Trance induction methodology", "tone_constraint": "Curious, permissive, and non-authoritarian", "structural_constraint": "Open-ended question focusing on the subject's internal cognitive process"}, "instruction": "Ask the subject about their method of inducing a trance in a way that encourages them to mentally simulate the experience, thereby initiating a light trance state through internal focus.", "reasoning_trace": "Erickson's goal is to bypass the subject's conscious resistance by using a 'meta-question.' Instead of telling the subject to enter a trance, he asks them to think about the process. To answer this question, the subject must access their internal representations of what a 'trance' is and how it feels. This internal search naturally leads to the very state being discussed. The phrase 'How do you think' shifts the responsibility to the subject's own intellect, making them an active participant in the hypnotic process. This is a classic example of 'utilization'—using the subject's own thoughts to facilitate the desired outcome. By focusing on the 'how,' the subject's mind moves away from 'whether' they will enter a trance, effectively bypassing the critical factor.", "output": "How do you think you would induce a trance?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_IDEOMOTOR_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Mechanism of ideomotor activity and internal focus shift", "tone_constraint": "Educational, hypnotic, and authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Direct observation followed by psychological linking and internal redirection"}, "instruction": "상호 암시 훈련을 마친 내담자들에게 관념운동(ideomotor) 반응의 원리를 설명하면서, 그 설명 과정 자체가 내담자의 주의를 내부로 돌리고 최면 상태를 심화시키도록 유도하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자들이 서로 지시를 주고받았던 실제 상황을 언급하여 현재의 경험을 긍정(Pacing)한다. Ideomotor activity. Your eyes are closing, and there is a tendency for you to close your own eyes; thus, you are offering suggestions, and you are meaning them. You are also learning something about the timing of suggestions. You suddenly discover that you are really interested in your own feeling, and when did you forget about her?"}

Disarming Inquiry: Start with 'What happened?' to invite the patient to notice their own transition without demanding a logical report. 2. Pacing Current Reality: State the obvious ('You just woke up') to align with the patient's immediate sensory experience. 3. Reframing: Label the trance as 'rest' ('Did you rest up a bit?') to ensure the patient views the experience as beneficial and safe. 4. Immediate Validation: Use 'That is fine' to provide unconditional clinical permission for their state of being. 5. Soft Directive: Transition to physical movement with a polite request ('Do you mind sitting up here?') which functions as a subtle command for re-alerting. 6. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Explanation of time distortion during hypnosis", "tone_constraint": "Conversational, reassuring, and subtly authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Begins with a rapport-building phrase followed by a universal truth (Truism)"}, "instruction": "내담자가 최면 상태에서 경험한 시간 왜곡 현상을 자연스럽고 당연한 것으로 받아들이게 하기 위해, 반박할 수 없는 보편적 진리(Truism)를 활용하여 설명하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 'Well, you know'라는 구절을 사용하여 내담자와 지식과 경험을 공유하고 있다는 친밀한 래포(Rapport)를 형성한다. 그 다음, 시간 왜곡이라는 주관적 경험을 '시간은 원래 눈에 띄지 않게 흘러가는 습성이 있다'는 객관적이고 보편적인 사실로 치환한다. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_NORMALIZATION_ANCHOR", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reducing patient isolation through historical continuity", "tone_constraint": "Factual, calm, and subtly empathetic", "structural_constraint": "Simple declarative sentence using spatial anchoring"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 고통이나 상황 속에서 고립감을 느끼지 않도록, 물리적 환경(의자)을 매개로 하여 이전 내담자들과의 연결성을 암시하는 밀턴 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 생성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 내담자의 고립감을 해소하기 위해 '보편성(Universality)'의 원리를 적용함. 나만 이런 문제를 겪는 것이 아니라는 안도감을 주고자 함. 둘째, 현재 내담자가 앉아 있는 '의자'라는 물리적 대상을 '공유된 경험의 장소'로 앵커링(Anchoring)함. 셋째, '어제(Yesterday)'라는 구체적인 시간을 언급하여 치료적 연속성을 강조함. 넷째, '또 다른 어머니(another mother)'라는 표현을 통해 내담자의 정체성(어머니로서의 고충 등)과 공명할 수 있는 대상을 제시함. 다섯째, 직접적인 위로 대신 단순한 사실(Truism)을 전달함으로써 내담자의 저항을 우회하고 무의식적으로 '나도 그들처럼 도움을 받을 수 있다'는 가능성을 수용하게 함.", "output": "Yesterday there was another mother sitting in that chair."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DOUBLE_BIND_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inducing comfort through social presence and presupposition", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, inquisitive, yet authoritative and leading", "structural_constraint": "Negative interrogative form used to embed a suggestion"}, "instruction": "무대 위의 두 내담자 중 한 명에게, 다른 한 명이 곁에 있다는 사실을 이용하여 자연스럽게 편안함을 느끼도록 유도하는 이중 구속(Double Bind) 질문을 던지세요.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 목표 설정: 내담자가 현재 느끼는 긴장을 완화하고 최면적 편안함(Comfort)을 수용하게 함. 2. 전제(Presupposition) 활용: '당신은 편안합니까?'라고 묻는 대신 '더 편안하지 않나요?'라는 부정 의문문을 사용하여, 이미 어느 정도 편안함이 존재한다는 사실을 전제로 깔아둠. 3. 이중 구속(Double Bind)의 변형: '예/아니오'의 선택을 '더 편안함'이라는 상태 안으로 가둠. 아니라고 대답하기에는 사회적 상황(옆에 동료가 있음)이 주는 안도감을 부정해야 하므로 무의식은 '편안함'을 선택하게 됨. 4. 외부 자극의 재구성: 옆에 있는 다른 피험자(she)의 존재를 '안전'과 '편안함'의 근거로 연결(Linkage)함. 이는 논리적 인과관계가 부족하더라도 무의식은 이를 타당한 이유로 받아들임. 5. 언어적 장치: 'a bit more'라는 표현을 통해 변화의 폭을 작게 설정하여 저항을 최소화함.", "output": "Aren’t you a bit more comfortable, knowing that she is up here?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRESUPPOSITION_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Enhancing subject comfort through social presence", "tone_constraint": "Calm, observational, and subtly authoritative", "structural_constraint": "A single sentence linking an external fact to an internal state using a causal bridge."}, "instruction": "Demonstrate how to use the presence of a second person on stage to deepen a subject's comfort by framing it as a presupposed fact.", "reasoning_trace": "To facilitate a deeper state of relaxation or comfort in a subject, I observe the immediate environment. Here, a second person is present. Instead of suggesting comfort directly, which might invite doubt, I link the comfort to the undeniable fact of the other person's presence. By saying 'knowing that you are up here,' I create a logical bridge that makes the comfort seem like a natural, inevitable consequence of the situation. This bypasses the critical faculty of the subject, as they cannot deny the other person is there, and thus they are more likely to accept the accompanying state of 'being more comfortable' as a true observation of their own internal experience.", "output": "And she is more comfortable, knowing that you are up here."}

'You don’t think you are very resistant'라는 표현은 내담자의 의식에는 동조하는 것처럼 보이지만, 무의식에는 '저항'이라는 키워드를 강력하게 주입하는 효과가 있습니다. 그 직후, 내담자가 이 논리에 대해 깊이 생각하거나 반박할 틈을 주지 않기 위해 '대중 앞에 앉아 있는 현재의 감각적/사회적 상황'으로 주의를 급격히 돌립니다. 이는 의식의 초점을 분산시켜 무의식이 암시를 수용하게 만드는 전형적인 에릭슨의 혼란 및 분리 기법입니다.", "output": "You don’t think you are very resistant. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ILLUSION_OF_CHOICE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Demonstrating resistance on stage", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, calm, and subtly challenging", "structural_constraint": "Short interrogative sentence using the presuppositional word 'try'"}, "instruction": "내담자가 무대 위에서 저항하는 모습을 보여주어야 하는 상황에서, 그 저항조차 최면가의 지시 범위 안에 가두어버리는 이중 구속(Double Bind)의 질문을 하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 '저항'이라는 상태를 수용(Pacing)하면서도 이를 통제(Leading)하기 위한 전략을 세웁니다. 'Try(시도하다)'라는 단어는 최면 언어학에서 매우 강력한 도구입니다. 무언가를 '시도하라'고 요청하는 것은 무의식적으로 '그것을 완수하지 못할 수도 있음' 또는 '노력하는 행위 자체'에 집중하게 만듭니다. 만약 내담자가 저항하려고 노력한다면 그는 이미 나의 '시도하라'는 지시를 따르고 있는 것이 됩니다. 즉, 저항에 성공하든 실패하든 내담자는 나의 프레임 안에 갇히게 됩니다. 질문 형식을 취함으로써 내담자의 비판적 사고를 우회하고, 그가 스스로 선택하여 저항을 '시도'하는 것처럼 느끼게 유도했습니다.", "output": "Would you try?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_RESISTANCE_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Resistance demonstration and induction", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, paradoxical, and validating", "structural_constraint": "Direct command followed by a challenge, validation of resistance, and a pattern-interrupting question."}, "instruction": "Create a scenario where you instruct a subject to resist your physical action (lifting their arm) to demonstrate how resistance can be utilized as a form of cooperation in a therapeutic or hypnotic context.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Initiate physical contact to ground the interaction and focus the subject's attention on a specific body part (the wrist). 2. Explicitly command the subject to resist ('Don't let me...'), which paradoxically makes their resistance a form of following instructions. This is a classic 'Double Bind' where whether they resist or comply, they are following the therapist's lead. 3. Increase the physical and psychological stakes by promising effort ('I will pull quite hard'), focusing their conscious mind entirely on the physical struggle. 4. Use the phrase 'That is right' to bridge the gap between their resistance and your control, suggesting that their struggle is exactly the desired outcome. 5. Conclude with a pattern-interrupting question ('What is the matter?') at the height of the physical tension to create a moment of cognitive disorientation, which facilitates a deeper trance state or increased suggestibility.", "output": "All right. I am going to take hold of your wrist and lift it up in the air. Don’t let me lift your arm up, but I will pull quite hard. I will get it up. That is right. What is the matter?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_AND_VALIDATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The pedagogical utilization of resistance in a clinical demonstration.", "tone_constraint": "Reassuring, authoritative, and instructional.", "structural_constraint": "Immediate validation of the subject followed by a rationalization for the audience's benefit."}, "instruction": "Explain to an audience why you encouraged a subject to demonstrate resistance, framing the resistance as a positive educational tool rather than a clinical failure.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Validation: Start with 'That is right' to immediately reinforce the subject's behavior. This prevents the subject from feeling self-conscious about their resistance and maintains rapport. 2. Positive Reinforcement: Use 'You did it very, very nicely' to transform a potentially negative behavior (resistance) into a successful performance. 3. Reframing: Shift the focus from the 'problem' of resistance to the 'lesson' of resistance. 4. Normalization: Use the phrase 'one doesn’t have to be troubled' to de-stigmatize resistance for both the subject and the observing practitioners. 5. Strategic Intent: Reveal that the resistance was a deliberate part of the demonstration, thereby maintaining therapeutic control while appearing to grant the subject autonomy.", "output": "That is right. You did it very, very nicely, because I wanted the audience to see how one doesn’t have to be troubled about resistance."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TEMPORAL_LINKAGE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Focusing attention and inducing selective amnesia regarding the audience.", "tone_constraint": "Observational, reinforcing, and authoritative yet gentle.", "structural_constraint": "A 'When X, Y' temporal bridge linking a physical sensation to a psychological shift."}, "instruction": "Generate a hypnotic suggestion that links a subject's physical sensation to the immediate forgetting of their surroundings using a temporal cause-and-effect structure.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve the goal of making the subject forget the audience, I must first identify a physiological marker of their trance state—in this case, the sensation of the arm 'getting big' (a common hypnotic distortion). By using the word 'When', I create a temporal link that makes the psychological result (forgetting the audience) seem like an inevitable consequence of the physical sensation. I frame the statement in the past tense ('started', 'forgot') to suggest that this shift has already successfully occurred, which bypasses the subject's critical faculty. Finally, adding the phrase 'just that quickly' reinforces the ease and speed of the process, validating the subject's experience and deepening the trance focus.", "output": "When your arm started to get big again, you forgot the audience just that quickly."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Redirecting attention by validating natural distractions", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, permissive, and rhythmically hypnotic", "structural_constraint": "Observation of behavior followed by scientific justification and rhythmic prediction"}, "instruction": "Explain the phenomenon of wandering attention to an audience in a way that utilizes their natural behavior and frames it as an inevitable psychological process, using Milton Erickson's conversational style.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve the goal of redirecting attention without resistance, I will first employ a 'Truism' by stating something the audience cannot deny—that their eyes have wandered. This builds 'Yes-Set' momentum. Next, I will provide a rational, scientific 'cushion' by mentioning psychological studies, which bypasses the critical mind by appealing to logic. I will then use the 'Utilization' technique, treating the distraction not as a problem but as a natural cycle. By using rhythmic repetition ('drift away... drift back'), I create a verbal cadence that mirrors the physical experience, effectively pacing their current state. Finally, I will frame this entire sequence as a 'simple, psychological fact' to solidify the suggestion that their return to focus is inevitable and natural.", "output": "Now, you have undoubtedly noticed that while you looked at the clock, your eyes showed a tendency to wander. Actually, of course, in all the psychological studies made of human attention, it has a very limited span. Therefore, I think you ought to be interested in noticing that your eyes drifted away, and sooner or later they will drift back; then they will drift away again, and then they will drift back. And I have stated a simple, psychological fact."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_REPETITIVE_PACING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Building a therapeutic frame with a resistant patient through sensory pacing and utilization.", "tone_constraint": "Rhythmic, monotonous, matter-of-fact, and non-confrontational.", "structural_constraint": "Repetitive listing of undeniable environmental facts (truisms) interspersed with the direct labeling of the patient's resistance."}, "instruction": "How would you use environmental pacing and the utilization of resistance to establish a hypnotic frame of reference for a patient who is consciously unwilling to cooperate?", "reasoning_trace": "First, I must establish a 'Yes-Set' by stating undeniable environmental truths (truisms) such as the chair, the picture, and the carpet. This bypasses the patient's critical faculty because they cannot disagree with sensory reality. Second, I use extreme repetition to create a rhythmic, almost boring cadence that encourages the conscious mind to wander or fatigue. Third, I utilize the patient's resistance directly by labeling it ('you are a resistant patient'). By doing this, I am pacing their current state; if they continue to resist, they are following my description of them, which is a form of rapport. Fourth, I weave these elements together—the physical objects and the internal state of resistance—into a single stream of experience. Finally, I shift the focus from the abstract concept of resistance back to concrete sensory experiences like the feeling of shoes on their feet, effectively grounding the hypnotic induction in the present moment and the physical body.", "output": "As you sit there in this chair, and you sit there in that chair, you will notice there is a picture on the wall there. There is a curtain there, and there is a doctor sitting there, and a doctor sitting there. There is a carpet on the floor, there is a tape recorder there and, of course, you are going to have difficulty cooperating with me in hypnosis because you are a resistant patient. You know it, and you are not quite certain about it. But there is a picture on the wall there, you couldn’t help noticing, and there is a curtain on the wall there, and there is a doctor there, and a doctor there, and a doctor there, and a picture there on the wall. And while you are sitting there in that chair with your feet on the floor just as easily as you see a picture on the wall, the doctor there, the doctor there, the curtain there, the picture there, the doctor there. And you can feel the shoes on your feet, and keep right on feeling the shoes on your feet until you direct your attention to the picture on the wall; and the doctor there and the doctor there, the picture there, the carpet on the floor and the tape recorder."}

'there'라는 단어의 반복적 사용은 리듬감을 형성하여 내담자의 의식을 이완시키고 무의식적 집중을 유도함.", "output": "And after a while you can literally see the doctor sitting there, and the doctor sitting there, and the doctor there, and the curtain on the wall, the picture there, the picture"}

'당신은 ~하고 싶을 것입니다'라는 표현을 통해 내담자의 욕구와 치료적 암시를 일치시켰습니다.", "output": "But, of course, it isn’t a question of your right hand or your left hand, your right elbow, your left elbow, or your right foot or your left foot. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_THERAPEUTIC_DOUBLE_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Resolving conflicting parental expectations through a therapeutic double bind", "tone_constraint": "Direct, authoritative yet collaborative, and paradoxically liberating", "structural_constraint": "Identification of existing negative binds followed by the introduction of a constructive, paradoxical alternative"}, "instruction": "Create a therapeutic intervention for a patient trapped between the conflicting demands of their parents, using Milton Erickson's technique of the 'therapeutic double bind' to grant the patient autonomy.", "reasoning_trace": "1. **Acknowledge the Existing Conflict**: First, I must explicitly identify the 'negative double binds' the patient is already experiencing. The father demands a job, the mother demands staying at home; both lead to disappointment. This validates the patient's feeling of being 'wrong' no matter what they do.\n2. **Meta-Communication**: I will openly state my intention to use a 'double bind' but frame it as being 'to your advantage.' This transparency shifts the power dynamic and invites the patient to collaborate in their own liberation.\n3. **Utilize Available Resources**: I look for external variables that can be manipulated—in this case, the family's two houses (city and country) and the flexibility of work hours.\n4. **Construct the Paradoxical Solution**: By suggesting the patient live in whichever house the parents are NOT in, and working a split schedule, I create a situation where the patient is technically fulfilling the requirements (working and living at home) while physically and psychologically avoiding the conflict. \n5. **Shift the Burden of 'Being Wrong'**: The goal is to flip the script so that instead of the patient being 'wrong,' the parents' rigid expectations become the source of the error. This restores the patient's sense of agency through a clever, structured avoidance.", "output": "You know, I would like to put you in a double bind, but I would like to put you in a double bind to your advantage. What kind of a double bind can we work out? You are in a double bind with your father, and you are in a double bind with your mother. Your father is going to insist that you take that job, and he is going to be as disappointed as can be. Your mother is going to insist that you live at home, and she is going to be as disappointed as can be if you do. Well, any way you are going to be wrong. All right, this is what you do: Fortunately your family owns both a country house and a city house. Live at home. While your parents are in the city house, you live in the country house; while they are in the country house, you live in the city house. Work half time on that job, one week in the forenoon; the next week in the afternoon. Your father is going to be wrong each way."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PARADOXICAL_COMPLIANCE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Handling overbearing parental demands through strategic agreement", "tone_constraint": "Calm, matter-of-fact, seemingly compliant but strategically subversive", "structural_constraint": "Repetitive acknowledgment of demands followed by a complex, multi-location execution plan"}, "instruction": "어머니의 과도한 통제와 요구에 시달리는 내담자에게, 저항 대신 '역설적 순응'을 통해 주도권을 되찾는 에릭슨식 대화 전략을 제시하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자가 어머니의 요구에 직접적으로 저항할 경우 발생하는 소모적 갈등을 피하기 위해 '이용(Utilization)' 기법을 선택함. 2. 어머니의 구체적인 요구사항들(식당, 대학, 과목)을 하나씩 긍정하며 'Yes-Set'을 형성하여 표면적인 순응의 분위기를 조성함. 3. '좋습니다(Fine)'라는 표현을 반복하여 어머니의 심리적 저항을 낮춤. 4. 실행 단계에서 요구사항을 문자 그대로 이행하되, 이를 물리적으로 분리(피닉스 대학과 애리조나 주립대 야간 학교)하여 실행하는 복잡한 조건을 추가함. 5. 이러한 복잡한 이행 방식은 어머니의 통제 범위를 벗어나게 만들며, 내담자가 요구를 수용하면서도 동시에 자신의 독립적인 행동 영역을 확보하는 역설적 효과를 노림.", "output": "어머니는 당신이 특정 식당에서 식사하기를 원하고, 특정 대학에 가기를 원하며, 특정 과목을 수강하기를 원하시죠. 그리고 당신이 그 세 가지 중 하나라도 행한다면 어머니는 실망하시게 될 겁니다. 그러니 어머니에게 이렇게 말씀하세요. '어머니, 제가 대학에 가길 원하시니 좋습니다. 특정 식당에서 밥을 먹으라 하시니 그것도 좋습니다. 특정 과목들을 들으라 하시니, 그 과목들을 신청하겠습니다. 저는 이 과목들을 피닉스 대학에서 수강하고, 나머지 과목들은 템피에 있는 애리조나 주립대학교 야간 학교에서 수강할 계획입니다.'"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PARADOXICAL_TASKING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Managing family sabotage and double binds in weight loss therapy", "tone_constraint": "Pragmatic, authoritative, yet seemingly collaborative and reasonable", "structural_constraint": "Direct intervention dialogue nested within a clinical explanation of the strategy"}, "instruction": "Explain how to resolve a situation where a parent is sabotaging a child's progress using a double bind, and provide the specific Erickson-style verbal intervention to redirect the parent's resistance.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I identify the 'horrible mess' of the double bind where the mother uses circular logic to force the child to eat. My goal is to bypass the mother's resistance not by opposing her, but by utilizing her need for control. I bring them together to establish a shared reality based on 'reasonableness' (height, average weight). Then, I employ a paradoxical intervention: I assign the mother the 'responsibility' of limiting the weight loss. By telling her 'do not let her lose more than X pounds,' I am actually prescribing and authorizing the weight loss itself. This shifts her role from a saboteur of the goal to a guardian of the limit, effectively giving the child permission to lose weight within those boundaries without maternal interference.", "output": "I know, that is a horrible mess. “You’ve got to eat to keep up your strength so you’ll have enough strength to lose weight.’’ What I usually do is get the mother and the child together. The mother doesn’t know what I am doing. I point out to the mother: “Now, listen, let’s be reasonable about this child’s loss of weight. How tall is your daughter? What do you think is the average weight? How much should she weigh? Well, let’s allow for an extra fifteen pounds, and I want you to see to it that she does not lose more than two and a half pounds a week, or not more than one pound a week. That is your responsibility, Mother, and you see to it that she doesn’t lose more than that.”"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DOUBLE_BIND_PROVOCATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Breaking resistance in a forced therapy session", "tone_constraint": "Provocative, challenging, and authoritative yet offering a pseudo-choice", "structural_constraint": "A binary choice (Double Bind) where both options lead to the initiation of communication"}, "instruction": "Generate a provocative opening statement for a resistant 20-year-old male client who was forced into therapy by his father, using a double bind that compels him to speak.", "reasoning_trace": "The client is present under duress, likely feeling powerless and resentful. To break this impasse, I must bypass his conscious resistance by creating a situation where silence is no longer a safe defense. I will use a 'Double Bind'—a hallmark of Ericksonian hypnosis. First, I acknowledge the inevitability of the session starting. Second, I offer two choices: starting voluntarily now, or waiting for a negative stimulus (an insult). By framing the insult as a consequence of waiting, I position myself not as a typical 'nice' therapist but as someone unpredictable and potentially 'dangerous,' which commands immediate attention. This shock tactic disrupts his defensive posture. Whether he chooses to start now to avoid the insult or reacts to the threat of an insult, he must engage with me. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DOUBLE_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Managing resistance through provocative engagement and the illusion of choice", "tone_constraint": "Calm, matter-of-fact, and playfully challenging", "structural_constraint": "A binary choice (A or B) that forces the subject to accept the underlying premise of the interaction"}, "instruction": "내담자가 모욕을 기다리겠다고 대답하며 수동적으로 저항하는 상황에서, 그가 저항을 멈추고 대화의 프레임에 완전히 몰입하도록 유도하는 이중 구속(Double Bind) 질문을 던지세요.", "reasoning_trace": "내담자가 '모욕을 기다리겠다'고 말한 것은 치료자의 다음 행동을 수동적으로 지켜보겠다는 저항의 일종이다. 에릭슨은 이 상황에서 내담자에게 '선택권'을 주는 척하면서 실제로는 치료적 통제권을 강화하는 전략을 취한다. '가벼운 모욕(mild insult)'과 '철저한 모욕(thorough-going insult)'이라는 두 가지 선택지를 제시함으로써, 내담자는 '모욕을 받을지 말지'를 결정하는 것이 아니라 '어떤 강도의 모욕을 받을지'를 고민하게 된다. 이 과정에서 내담자는 자신도 모르게 '모욕을 받는다'는 전제(Premise)를 수용하게 되며, 이는 치료자와의 상호작용에 깊이 관여하게 만드는 결과를 낳는다. 지극히 평범한 질문처럼 던짐으로써 내담자의 방어 기제를 우회하고 호기심과 긴장감을 동시에 유발한다.", "output": "Well, do you want a mild insult, or do you want thorough-going insult?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DOUBLE_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Initiating a provocative therapeutic intervention (Insult Process)", "tone_constraint": "Provocative, authoritative, yet cryptic and playful", "structural_constraint": "A binary choice (Double Bind) that presupposes the inevitable occurrence and completion of a process"}, "instruction": "내담자가 거부감을 느낄 수 있는 도발적인 치료 기법을 시작하기 전, 내담자의 저항을 무력화하고 통제권을 부여하는 듯한 착각을 주면서도 치료자의 의도대로 상황을 이끌어가는 '이중 구속(Double Bind)' 질문을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자의 의식적 자아는 '모욕'이나 '도발'에 대해 방어 기제를 작동시킬 가능성이 높음. 2. 따라서 질문의 초점을 '과정의 실행 여부'가 아닌 '과정의 종료를 인지하는 방식'으로 옮겨야 함. 3. '내가 말해줄 것인가(외부적 단서)'와 '당신이 추측할 것인가(내부적 단서)'라는 두 가지 선택지를 제시함. 4. 내담자가 어떤 선택을 하든, '과정은 이미 시작되었고 반드시 끝날 것'이라는 전제(Presupposition)를 무의식적으로 수용하게 만듦. 5. '추측(guess)'이라는 단어를 통해 내담자의 무의식을 자극하여 치료자의 반응을 예민하게 관찰하게 유도함.", "output": "Shall I tell you when I am through, or do you just want to guess?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ANALOGY_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Frequency of autohypnosis practice", "tone_constraint": "Pragmatic, authoritative yet relatable, and grounded in common sense.", "structural_constraint": "Starts with a universal truism, followed by a vivid sensory analogy (steak), and concludes with a strategic limitation."}, "instruction": "Explain to a patient why they should use autohypnosis selectively rather than constantly, using a common physical analogy to make the point memorable and to preserve the technique's effectiveness.", "reasoning_trace": "To ensure the patient maintains the potency of the hypnotic state, I must prevent it from becoming a mundane habit. By illustrating the absurdity of eating steak for every meal, I create a psychological association where 'too much' equals 'loss of value'. This allows the patient to internalize the need for moderation without feeling restricted by the therapist. Finally, I bridge the analogy back to autohypnosis, framing the instruction not as a prohibition, but as a way to 'not waste' a valuable resource on trivial matters, thereby elevating the perceived importance of the technique when it is actually used.", "output": "Never wear out a good thing. You get fed up with anything that you have too frequently. So I am going to teach you autohypnosis, but don’t waste it on every little thing that comes along."}

Relax and get all those general feelings; give your body a chance to learn, because otherwise you are going to interfere with yourself. If you want to learn to target shoot, you aim at the target and you pull the trigger. Then you reload, you aim comfortably at the target, and you shoot again. You reload, aim comfortably at the target, and shoot again. But if you load and dart down to the target, come back disappointed, load, and desperately shoot again, and dash down to the target, then you are going to interfere with the learning process of hitting the target. You need to assume that you are getting closer and closer to the bull’s-eye, and that feeling of comfort that you have enables you to have increasing control of your physiological processes."}

'무엇에 대한 것인지 모른다'는 표현은 공포의 실체를 모호하게 만들어 그 영향력을 약화시키고, '얼마나 오래 지속할지 모른다'는 표현은 공포가 결국 '종결될 것'이라는 강력한 전제(Presupposition)를 심는다. 이는 내담자가 공포를 영구적인 것이 아닌, 언젠가 끝날 기간 한정적인 현상으로 재구조화하도록 유도하는 고도의 언어적 계산이다.", "output": "But certainly you will have an unreasoning fear, and I don’t know about what. In fact, I don’t know how long you are going to keep it."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reframing pregnancy fear into practical preparation", "tone_constraint": "Calm, authoritative, and matter-of-fact", "structural_constraint": "Future-oriented presupposition combined with a truism"}, "instruction": "임신에 대한 두려움을 가진 내담자에게, 그 불안을 실질적이고 긍정적인 선택의 과정으로 재구조화(Reframing)하여 전달하십시오. 내담자가 거부감을 느끼지 않도록 당연한 사실(Truism)과 전제(Presupposition)를 활용하여 미래의 행동을 유도하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 느끼는 '두려움'이라는 감정의 에너지를 '신중함(thoughtful)'이라는 생산적인 상태로 재정의(Reframing)합니다. 'It is going to make you...'라는 구문을 사용하여 임신이라는 상황이 이미 진행 중이며, 그 결과로 내담자가 특정 행동을 하게 될 것임을 자연스럽게 전제(Presupposition)합니다. 내담자의 주의를 추상적인 공포에서 '산과 의사 선택'과 '병원 결정'이라는 구체적이고 통제 가능한 행동으로 전환시킵니다. 마지막으로 'and, of course'라는 삽입구를 통해 좋은 병원을 선택하는 것이 너무나 당연하고 필연적인 수순임을 암시하여 내담자의 무의식이 저항 없이 긍정적인 미래상을 받아들이도록 설계했습니다.", "output": "It is going to make you rather thoughtful in selecting your obstetrician and, of course, you will choose a good hospital."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DOUBLE_BIND_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Preparing for a baby's arrival (layette preparation)", "tone_constraint": "Calm, matter-of-fact, and subtly authoritative yet permissive.", "structural_constraint": "Use of a 'yes-set' opening followed by a choice between two alternatives that both lead to the desired action."}, "instruction": "임신 중인 내담자가 아기 용품을 준비하는 과정에서 느낄 수 있는 심리적 부담을 완화하면서, 준비라는 행동 자체를 당연한 일상적 흐름으로 받아들이도록 유도하는 최면적 제안을 하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 'And, of course'라는 문구로 시작하여 내담자의 현재 상황과 앞으로 일어날 일을 기정사실화하는 'Yes-set'을 형성함. 2. 'making the layette, or buying one'이라는 이중 구속(Double Bind) 기법을 사용함. 내담자에게 '직접 만들 것인가' 아니면 '살 것인가'라는 선택권을 부여함으로써, '준비를 할 것인가 말 것인가'라는 근본적인 저항을 우회하고 준비라는 행위 자체에 집중하게 함. 3. 'reasonably good'이라는 모호한 형용사를 사용하여 내담자가 자신의 기준에 맞춰 '적당함'을 정의하게 함으로써, 완벽주의적 불안감을 해소하고 실행 가능성을 높임. 4. 'you see to it'이라는 표현을 통해 내담자에게 통제권과 책임감을 부여하여 무의식적인 유능감을 자극함.", "output": "And, of course, in making the layette, or buying one, you see to it that it is a reasonably good layette."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DISPLACEMENT_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reframing pregnancy anxiety through specific physical focus and personality utilization", "tone_constraint": "Curious, wondering, slightly provocative, and clinical", "structural_constraint": "Repetitive questioning, shifting from general curiosity to a specific confrontation with the patient's personality trait"}, "instruction": "Write a therapeutic dialogue where you help a pregnant patient manage her generalized anxiety by displacing her focus onto a specific physical change, such as breast development, and utilizing her own personality traits (like being 'unreasoning') to challenge her mindset.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I establish a temporal bridge with 'As your pregnancy develops' to link the suggestion to the natural passage of time. Second, I use the 'I wonder' technique, which is a classic indirect suggestion that bypasses conscious resistance by appearing as a mere expression of my own curiosity rather than a command. Third, I employ the principle of displacement; instead of addressing the vast, overwhelming fear of 'pregnancy' or 'childbirth,' I narrow the focus to a specific, manageable physical change—the breasts. Fourth, I use repetition ('I really wonder') to deepen the patient's internal search. Finally, I utilize the patient's own known characteristic of being 'unreasoning' about things. By asking if she will take an 'unreasoning attitude' about this specific change, I force her to confront her own psychological patterns, making her anxiety a matter of personal 'attitude' rather than an external, uncontrollable force.", "output": "As your pregnancy develops, I wonder what sort of an attitude you are going to take about the changes in your breasts? And I really wonder. What kind of an attitude are you going to take about the changes in your breasts? What does that mean? You are the kind of a person who takes an unreasoning attitude on some things. Are you going to take an unreasoning attitude about your breasts?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Managing pregnancy fears through practical focus", "tone_constraint": "Pragmatic, authoritative, and reassuringly logical", "structural_constraint": "A cause-effect linkage connecting a universal biological concern to specific behavioral tasks"}, "instruction": "임신에 대한 막연한 불안감을 가진 내담자에게, 그 불안의 에너지를 구체적이고 관리 가능한 신체적 건강 관리 행동으로 전환시키기 위해 밀턴 에릭슨의 방식으로 조언하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 거부할 수 없는 생리적 사실(임신 중 칼슘 소모)을 'Truism(자명한 이치)'으로 제시하여 무의식적 동의를 얻어냅니다. '당신은 분명 ~을 원치 않을 것입니다'라는 표현은 내담자의 자기 보호 본능을 자극합니다. 그 후 '그러므로(so)'라는 접속사를 사용하여, 막연한 공포를 치과 방문과 식단 관리라는 매우 구체적이고 통제 가능한 행동으로 연결합니다. 이는 내담자의 주의(attention)를 통제 불가능한 '공포'에서 통제 가능한 '관리'로 재프레임(Reframing)하여 불안을 해소하는 전략적 개입입니다.", "output": "you certainly don’t want the calcium to be depleted, so you will see your dentist and you will watch your diet."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_QUESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Subject-led trance induction", "tone_constraint": "Curious, collaborative, and subtly presuppositional", "structural_constraint": "Open-ended question that presupposes the inevitability of the trance state"}, "instruction": "내담자가 최면 유도 과정에 능동적으로 참여하게 함으로써 저항을 무력화하고, 최면이 일어날 것이라는 전제를 자연스럽게 수용하게 만드는 밀턴 에릭슨의 질문 기법을 구현하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 목표 설정: 내담자의 비판적 사고(Critical Factor)를 우회하여 최면 유도에 대한 저항을 최소화함. 2. 전략 선택: 에릭슨의 '활용(Utilization)' 원칙을 적용. 내담자의 주관적 기대와 지식을 유도 전략의 기초로 삼음. 3. 언어적 장치: 'How do you think'라는 질문 형식을 통해 내담자에게 통제권을 주는 듯 보이지만, 실제로는 '내가 당신을 최면에 걸 것이다(putting you in a trance)'라는 사실을 기정사실화(Presupposition)함. 4. 심리적 기제: 내담자가 '방법'에 대해 고민하는 동안, '최면에 걸린다'는 결과는 무의식적으로 수용됨. 또한 내담자 자신의 아이디어를 사용함으로써 유도 과정에 대한 심리적 거부감을 없앰. 5. 최종 문장 구성: 정중하면서도 확신에 찬 어조로 내담자의 내부 자원을 이끌어냄.", "output": "How do you think I ought to go about putting you in a trance?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PARADOXICAL_REFRAME", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Relaxation and Tension Management", "tone_constraint": "Calm, authoritative, yet inquisitive and subtly challenging.", "structural_constraint": "Direct statement of intent followed by a paradoxical rhetorical question."}, "instruction": "내담자가 이완을 원할 때, 현재의 긴장 상태를 부정하지 않고 오히려 그 가치를 묻는 역설적 개입을 통해 저항을 우회하고 깊은 이완으로 유도하는 에릭슨의 화법을 구사하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. **목표 동조(Pacing)**: 내담자가 원하는 '이완'을 언급하며 치료적 동맹을 확인한다. '지금보다 더 이완시켜야겠다'는 선언은 미래의 변화를 예고하는 강력한 암시가 된다. 2. **대조의 원리**: '지금보다 더'라는 표현을 통해 현재 상태와 미래 상태를 분리하며 변화의 필연성을 부여한다. 3. **역설적 개입(Paradoxical Intervention)**: 긴장을 없애야 할 적이 아니라, 가끔은 '좋은 것'으로 재정의(Reframing)한다. 내담자가 긴장을 풀려고 애쓰는 의식적 노력을 중단시키기 위함이다. 4. **저항 활용(Utilization)**: 긴장을 긍정함으로써 내담자가 긴장에 대해 느끼는 불안이나 저항을 무력화한다. '긴장하는 것도 괜찮다'는 허용은 역설적으로 긴장을 유지할 동기를 상실하게 만들어 자연스러운 이완을 이끈다. 5. **수사적 질문**: '~하지 않나요?'라는 질문 형식은 내담자의 무의식이 긴장의 긍정적 측면을 탐색하게 만들며, 이 과정에서 의식의 비판적 사고를 우회한다.", "output": "I will have to get you more relaxed than you are right now. Don’t you think it is nice to be tense once in a while?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PACING_AND_LEADING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inducing trance through sensory focus on contact lenses", "tone_constraint": "Repetitive, rhythmic, and paradoxically authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Initial focus on conscious wakefulness followed by a sudden shift to sensory awareness and eye closure"}, "instruction": "내담자가 콘택트렌즈라는 구체적인 사물에 집중하게 유도하면서, '완전히 깨어 있으라'는 역설적 지시를 반복하여 의식을 포화시킨 뒤, 자연스럽게 눈을 감고 신체 감각에 몰입하도록 유도하는 에릭슨의 최면 유도문을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 주의를 콘택트렌즈라는 물리적 실체에 고정시킵니다. '깨어 있으라'는 지시를 반복적으로 사용함으로써 내담자의 의식적 저항을 무력화하는 역설적 기법(Paradoxical Suggestion)을 적용합니다. 반복적인 문구는 의식적인 사고를 지치게 만드는 '포화(Saturation)' 효과를 노린 것입니다. 이후 'That is right'라는 긍정적 강화를 통해 내담자의 상태를 수용하고, 시선을 외부(렌즈에 대한 생각)에서 내부(눈꺼풀 아래의 감각)로 전환시킵니다. 마지막으로 렌즈의 이물감을 눈을 감아야 할 물리적 이유로 활용하여, 깨어 있으라는 명령에서 눈을 감으라는 명령으로 자연스럽게 이행(Leading)합니다.", "output": "All right. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REORIENTATION_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Awakening from trance and session termination", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, gentle, and grounded in reality", "structural_constraint": "Temporal truism followed by a permissive suggestion and an open-ended inquiry"}, "instruction": "세션이 끝나갈 때 내담자를 최면 상태에서 깨우기 위한 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 작성하세요. 시간의 흐름을 언급하는 자명한 이치(Truism)를 사용하고, 강요하지 않는 허용적 암시를 포함해야 합니다.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 '시간이 다 되었다'는 거부할 수 없는 사실(Truism)을 제시하여 내담자의 의식을 현재의 물리적 현실로 부드럽게 유도합니다. 그 다음, '눈을 떠라'는 명령 대신 '눈을 뜰 수 있다'는 허용적 어조(Permissive suggestion)를 사용하여 내담자의 자율성을 존중하면서도 자연스러운 각성을 유도합니다. 마지막으로, '기분이 어떠냐'는 개방형 질문을 던짐으로써 최면 중의 경험을 의식으로 통합하고 현재 상태를 확인하는 과정을 거칩니다. 'How did they look?'이라는 질문은 단순해 보이지만, 내담자로 하여금 자신의 기억 창고를 뒤져 시각적 정보를 인출하게 만드는 강력한 '트랜스 유도 질문'입니다. 이 질문은 내담자가 '그들이 어떻게 보였는지'를 설명하기 위해 필연적으로 시각적 표상 체계(Visual Representational System)를 활성화하게 하며, 이 과정에서 내담자는 최면적 몰입 상태로 자연스럽게 진입하게 됩니다. 구체적인 형용사를 제시하지 않음으로써 내담자의 무의식이 스스로 의미 있는 정보를 선택하도록 허용하는 '허용적 접근'이 핵심입니다.", "output": "How did they look?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_IDEOMOTOR_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Ideomotor signaling and conscious-unconscious dissociation", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, calm, and dissociative", "structural_constraint": "Utilizing childhood learning (nodding/shaking) to bypass conscious control"}, "instruction": "내담자에게 의식과 무의식을 분리시키고, 어린 시절 학습한 고개 끄덕임과 가로저음이라는 불수의적 반응(Ideomotor signaling)을 활용하여 무의식의 답변을 유도하는 대화를 구성하십시오. 특히 내담자가 의식적으로 답하지 않도록 주의를 주고, 무의식의 답변을 기다리는 과정을 포함해야 합니다.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 의식적인 답변을 명시적으로 거부함으로써 의식의 개입을 차단하고 무의식의 영역을 확보한다. 그 후 '고개 끄덕임'과 '가로저음'이라는, 모든 인간이 어린 시절 습득한 자동화된 신체 반응(Truism)을 언급하여 무의식이 소통할 수 있는 물리적 경로를 재활성화(Utilization)한다. '의식은 답을 모르지만 무의식은 안다'는 암시를 통해 의식과 무의식을 철저히 이원화(Dissociation)하고, '당신도 기다리고 나도 기다린다'는 표현으로 수행에 대한 압박을 제거하여 자율 신경계의 반응이 자연스럽게 나타나도록 유도한다. 마지막으로 트랜스 상태 여부를 묻는 폐쇄형 질문을 던져 무의식의 즉각적인 신체적 확인을 이끌어낸다.", "output": "좋습니다. 이제 당신에게 질문을 하나 하려고 합니다. 나는 당신이 의식적으로 대답하는 것을 원치 않습니다. 당신도 알다시피, 아주 오래전에 당신은 '예'라고 할 때는 고개를 끄덕이고 '아니오'라고 할 때는 고개를 젓는 법을 배웠습니다. 그렇습니다. 이제 나는 당신의 무의식에게 질문을 던질 것입니다. 의식적으로 당신은 무의식이 내놓을 그 답을 알지 못합니다. 당신은 당신의 의식적인 답변만을 알고 있죠. 그것은 내가 원하는 것이 아닙니다. 그래서 나는 당신의 무의식에게 특정한 질문을 던질 것이고, 당신과 나는 당신의 무의식이 대답하기를 함께 기다릴 것입니다. 그러면 당신의 무의식은 고개를 끄덕이거나 가로저음으로써 대답할 것입니다. 이제 내가 당신의 무의식에게 던질 질문은 이것입니다. 당신은 트랜스 상태에 있었습니까?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_IDEOMOTOR_YES_SET", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Subjective validation and ideomotor response induction", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, rhythmic, and progressively directive", "structural_constraint": "Validation -> Tag Question -> Ideomotor Suggestion -> Reinforcement"}, "instruction": "Elicit a physical ideomotor response from the subject by first validating their internal experience and then guiding them to respond through a slow head nod to confirm their state of trance.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve the desired psychological effect, I will begin by using a 'Yes-set' technique. By stating 'That is right,' I immediately validate the subject's current reality, reducing resistance. I then acknowledge their internal 'feeling' to bridge their conscious awareness with their unconscious experience. Using a tag question ('Isn't that right?') forces a mental 'yes.' I then transition from verbal agreement to a physical ideomotor response—a slow head nod. This bypasses conscious deliberation and utilizes the body's unconscious motor system. By asking 'Have you been in a trance?' while directing the nod, I link the physical movement to the recognition of the hypnotic state itself, reinforcing the trance through a feedback loop of suggestion and physical action.", "output": "That is right. You had the feeling. Isn’t that right? Now this time let your head nod slowly in answer to that question. Have you been in a trance? Slowly, let your head nod."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_AMNESIA_LINKING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inducing amnesia through temporal bridging", "tone_constraint": "Conversational, mundane, and seemingly inconsequential", "structural_constraint": "A simple interrogative sentence used as a psychological bookend"}, "instruction": "Explain the strategic use of a mundane question to facilitate post-hypnotic amnesia by linking the pre-trance and post-trance states.", "reasoning_trace": "To induce amnesia, I must create a psychological 'bridge' that bypasses the trance experience. I start by selecting a completely ordinary topic, such as the weather, which the conscious mind considers trivial. By asking 'Is it very hot outside today?' immediately before the induction, I establish a specific conscious-state anchor. After the trance work is complete, I repeat the exact same question the moment the patient opens their eyes. This creates a temporal 'short-circuit' where the patient's mind associates the second instance of the question with the first, effectively 'zipping' the two moments together and causing the intervening trance period to drop out of conscious awareness. The simplicity of the question is its strength; it does not trigger the critical faculty, allowing the amnesia to occur naturally and effortlessly.", "output": "Is it very hot outside today?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_AMNESIA", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inducing post-hypnotic amnesia through the utilization of mundane reality.", "tone_constraint": "Casual, objective, and matter-of-fact.", "structural_constraint": "A single, undeniable statement of environmental fact used as a psychological boundary."}, "instruction": "Explain how to use a simple truism about the weather to facilitate amnesia for a trance state, mimicking Milton Erickson's style.", "reasoning_trace": "To induce amnesia for the therapeutic work done in trance, I must create a sharp cognitive boundary between the 'trance state' and the 'waking state'. I will use a 'Truism'—a statement so obviously true that the conscious mind accepts it immediately and shifts its focus to the external environment. By mentioning the heat in Phoenix, I am re-orienting the patient to the physical 'here and now'. This mundane observation acts as a psychological 'bracket', signaling to the unconscious that the specialized work is concluded, while the conscious mind is occupied with a boring, everyday fact. This shift in context makes the preceding trance experiences less accessible to the conscious memory, effectively 'burying' the suggestions where they can work autonomously without conscious interference.", "output": "It is usually hot outside in Phoenix in the summertime."}

You really don’t want to injure your eyeballs when you don’t know what feelings are really harmful; what feelings aren’t just a little bit different. Actually, of course, I think your unconscious mind will be able to make that analysis for you, and I think your unconscious mind can accustom you to the sensation of contact lenses. And I am very certain that your unconscious mind will detect any little change or something bad in the feel. You think that might be comfortable? All right. Now take it easily and gradually.
